<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:United_Kingdom" title="Portal:United Kingdom">United Kingdom&#32;portal</a>  <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li>
<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of the United Kingdom">Atlas</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Template:Politics of the United Kingdom"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Template talk:Politics of the United Kingdom"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There are six types of <b>elections in the United Kingdom</b>: elections to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons" title="House of Commons">House of Commons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, elections to devolved parliaments and assemblies, elections to the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, local elections, mayoral elections and <a href="/wiki/Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="Police and Crime Commissioner">Police and Crime Commissioner</a> elections. Within each of those categories, there may be by-elections as well as general elections. Elections are held on <a href="/wiki/Election_Day_(United_Kingdom)" title="Election Day (United Kingdom)">Election Day</a>, which is conventionally a Thursday. Since the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Fixed-term_Parliaments_Act_2011" title="Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011">Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011</a> for general elections, all six types of elections are held after fixed periods, though early elections to parliament and the devolved assemblies and parliaments can occur in certain situations. Currently, six <a href="/wiki/Electoral_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral systems">electoral systems</a> are used: the <a href="/wiki/Single_member_plurality" class="mw-redirect" title="Single member plurality">single member plurality system</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Plurality-at-large_voting" title="Plurality-at-large voting">multi member plurality system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mixed_Member_Proportional" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed Member Proportional">additional member system</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplementary vote">supplementary vote</a>.
</p><p>Elections are administered locally: in each <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">lower-tier local authority</a>, the polling procedure is operated by the Acting Returning Officer or <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">Returning Officer</a>, and the compiling and maintenance of the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_roll" title="Electoral roll">electoral roll</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> (except in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Office_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Electoral Office for Northern Ireland">Electoral Office for Northern Ireland</a> assumes both responsibilities). The <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> sets standards for and issues guidelines to Returning Officers and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officers</a>, and is responsible for nationwide electoral administration (such as the registration of political parties and directing the administration of national referendums).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_registration">Electoral registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Electoral registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The total number of names in the United Kingdom appearing in Electoral Registers published on 1 December 2010 and based on a qualifying date of 15 October 2010 was 45,844,691.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entitlement_to_register">Entitlement to register</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Entitlement to register">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, anyone who will be aged 18 or over on polling day<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and who is a national of the United Kingdom (all forms of <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">British nationality</a> but excluding <a href="/wiki/British_protected_person" title="British protected person">British protected persons</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>), the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> country (including <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the <i>whole</i> of Cyprus <sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>) or a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> Member State,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> can apply to the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Local_government#United_Kingdom" title="Local government">local authority area</a> where they reside with a 'considerable degree of permanence'<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> to be listed in that area's Electoral Register.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, those fulfilling the nationality requirements (as stated in the previous paragraph) who will be aged 16 or over on polling day can register to vote, as the age for voting in <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Scotland#Scottish_Parliament" title="Elections in Scotland">Scottish Parliament</a> and local elections is 16. However, voters in Scotland under 18 are not entitled to vote in European Parliament and UK general elections.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A person can still register at their ordinary address if they will be away temporarily (for example, away working, on holiday, in student accommodation or in hospital).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A person who has two homes (such as a university student who has a term-time address and lives at home during holidays) may be able to register to vote at both addresses as long as they are not in the same electoral area<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> (though an elector can only vote once in any single election or referendum).
</p><p>In addition, to qualify to appear on the Electoral Register, applicants who are <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_citizen" title="Commonwealth citizen">Commonwealth citizens</a> must either possess <a href="/wiki/Leave_to_enter" title="Leave to enter">leave to enter or remain</a> in the UK or <a href="/wiki/Right_of_abode_(United_Kingdom)" title="Right of abode (United Kingdom)">not require such leave</a> on the date of their application<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and no applicant may be a convicted person detained in prison or a mental hospital (or unlawfully at large if they would otherwise have been detained)<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> or a person found guilty of certain corrupt or illegal practices.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, a further criterion has to be fulfilled to qualify for registration: it is possible for a person to apply to be listed on the Electoral Register only if they have been resident in Northern Ireland for at least three months prior to the date of application.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Remand prisoners, voluntary patients in mental hospitals and people without a fixed place of residence can register to vote by making a <b>declaration of local connection</b>.
</p><p>Members of <a href="/wiki/HM_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Forces">HM Forces</a> and their immediate family members have the option of registering as a <b>service voter</b>, by making a service declaration based on their last UK address.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_citizens" class="mw-redirect" title="British citizens">British citizens</a> (but not other categories of British nationals) residing outside the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> can register as an <b>overseas voter</b> provided that they were on the Electoral Register in the UK within the previous 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The 15-year period begins when they no longer appeared in the electoral register, not the date they moved abroad. British citizens who moved abroad before they turned 18 years old can still qualify for registration, with the 15-years period calculated from the date their parent(s)/guardian ceased to appear in the Electoral Register. Overseas voters can only vote in <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> and UK Parliamentary elections in the constituency of their last registered UK address (or for those who moved abroad as a minor, the last registered UK address of their parent(s)/guardian). British citizens who are away overseas temporarily do not need to register as overseas electors and can register to vote in the usual way at their UK address.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Crown_servant" title="Crown servant">Crown servants</a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/British_Council" title="British Council">British Council</a> employees<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> (as well as their spouses who live abroad<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>) employed in a post outside the UK can register by making a <b>Crown Servant declaration</b>, allowing them to vote in all UK elections.
</p><p>An individual can register as an <b><a href="/wiki/Anonymous_elector" title="Anonymous elector">anonymous elector</a></b> if his/her safety (or that of any other person in the same household) would be at risk were his/her name and address to be disclosed publicly on the Electoral Register, but the application needs to be supported by a relevant court order, injunction or an attestation by a <a href="/wiki/Chief_police_officer" title="Chief police officer">chief police officer</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Social_care_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Social care in the United Kingdom">Director of Social Services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The right of Commonwealth and Irish citizens to vote is a legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1918" title="Representation of the People Act 1918">Representation of the People Act 1918</a>, which limited the vote to British subjects. At that time, "British subjects" included the people of Ireland — then part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a> — and all other parts of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. Though most of Ireland (see <a href="/wiki/Ireland_Act_1949" title="Ireland Act 1949">Ireland Act 1949</a>) and the majority of the colonies became independent nations, their citizens have retained the right to vote if they live in the United Kingdom.
</p><p>In theory, members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a> who are not members of the House of Lords (including those who are peers who lost their right to sit following the House of Lords Act 1999) are eligible to vote, although in practice they do not exercise that right.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Registration_procedure">Registration procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Registration procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electoral_registration_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Electoral registration in the United Kingdom">Electoral registration in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, most electors are enrolled during the course of the <b>annual canvass</b>, which <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officers</a> are obliged to conduct every year between August and November.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Canvass forms are sent to all households, and must be returned, otherwise a fine of £1000 can be imposed.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> One person in the household must confirm the details of all residents who are existing electors, which includes adding or deleting residents who have moved in or out and are eligible to register to vote.
</p><p>Between December and early August, the <b>rolling registration</b> procedure applies instead. Applications must be submitted individually (unlike the annual canvass forms where one person is responsible for registering all eligible people in a household) using registration forms available from local Electoral Registration Officers or the Electoral Commission's website <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.aboutmyvote.co.uk">[4]</a>. Although no proof of identity or address is necessary when submitting an application, the Electoral Registration Officer can require the applicant to provide further <i>information</i> regarding the applicant's age, nationality, residence and whether or not they are disqualified<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and/or <i>evidence</i> to prove the applicant's age and/or nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Application forms can be returned to the local Electoral Registration Officer by post, by fax or by e-mail as a scanned attachment.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of June 2014, as part of the Government's Digital By Default policy, voters in England and Wales can register to the electoral roll online.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Special category electors do not register through the annual canvass procedure.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Instead, they submit applications at any time during the year and have to renew their electoral application periodically (every one year for overseas electors and voters with a declaration of local connection and every three years for service voters).
</p><p>After applications are received by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a>, he/she must add them to a list of applications (unless they are applications to register as an anonymous elector<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>). The list is open for inspection for five working days, during which any other elector may raise an objection to an application. The Electoral Registration Officer can initiate an <b>application hearing</b> if he/she considers that there are reasonable integrity concerns about the application.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, there is no annual canvass, and instead people register individually at any time during the year. Applicants must supply their <a href="/wiki/National_Insurance" title="National Insurance">National Insurance</a> number or, if they do not have one, make a declaration to that effect. Proof of identity, address, three months' residency in NI and date of birth must also be included with applications,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> which are submitted by post to the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Office_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Electoral Office for Northern Ireland">Electoral Office for Northern Ireland</a>.
</p><p>Knowingly giving false information to an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> anywhere in the UK is an offence with a maximum penalty, upon conviction, of £5000 and/or six months' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_Register">Electoral Register</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electoral Register">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Each <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_England" title="Districts of England">district council</a> or <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> has an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Register">Electoral Register</a> which is compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> listing all registered electors. The <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Register">Electoral Register</a> contains the name, qualifying address and electoral number of every ordinary elector, the name of every special category elector (such as service voters) and the electoral number of every anonymous elector. Any elector who was not aged 18 yet at the time of registration will also have his/her date of birth printed. Each district's <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Register">Electoral Register</a> is subdivided into separate registers for each polling district.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Because the franchise differs between individual voters, various markers may be placed next to voters' names to identify in which elections they are entitled to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> citizens who are not <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth" title="Commonwealth">Commonwealth</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Irish</a> citizens have their entry prefixed either with <b>G</b> (meaning they can only vote in local government elections) or <b>K</b> (meaning they can only vote in European Parliamentary and local government elections). Overseas electors are prefixed with the letter <b>F</b>, meaning they can only vote in European and UK Parliamentary elections. Members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> residing in the UK are prefixed with the letter <b>L</b>, meaning they can only vote in European Parliamentary and local government elections, whilst peers who are overseas electors are prefixed with the letter <b>E</b>, indicating that they can only vote in European Parliamentary elections.
</p><p>The Register is published every year on 1 December after the annual canvass period<sup id="cite_ref-representation1983_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-representation1983-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> (unless there has been an election during the annual canvass period between 1 July and 1 December,<sup id="cite_ref-representation1983_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-representation1983-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> in which case the publication date is 1 February in the following year<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>). However, in 2012, because the <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales_Police_and_Crime_Commissioner_elections,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="England and Wales Police and Crime Commissioner elections, 2012">Police and Crime Commissioner elections</a> were held on 15 November, the annual canvass in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> (excluding <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>) was held between July and October and the Electoral Register was published on 16 October.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Between January and September, during the 'rolling registration' period, notices of alteration are published on the first working day of each month to add, remove or amend names. Notices of alteration are also published 5 working days before an election at any time of the year<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and just before the close of poll at any election to correct any clerical errors or to implement any court decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> With the exception of a deceased elector who is removed from the Register, any individual who is added or removed from the Register must be notified by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are two versions of the Register: the full Register and the edited Register. The full Register can only be inspected under supervision at the office of the local Electoral Registration Officer, and must be supplied free of charge to the district's <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">Returning Officer</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> (only English and Welsh Registers), the <a href="/wiki/General_Register_Office_for_Scotland" title="General Register Office for Scotland">General Register Office for Scotland</a> (only Scottish Registers), the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Wales" title="National Library of Wales">National Library of Wales</a> (only English and Welsh Registers), the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Scotland" title="National Library of Scotland">National Library of Scotland</a> (only English and Scottish Registers) and the relevant <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Commissions_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary Commissions (United Kingdom)">Boundary Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The edited Register is available for general sale from Electoral Registration Officers and can be used for any purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Electors can choose to opt out from appearing in the edited Register by informing their local Electoral Registration Officer.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Party_system">Party system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Party system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg/220px-Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg/330px-Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg/440px-Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hustings_Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_20050204.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pre-election <a href="/wiki/Husting" title="Husting">husting</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_West_and_Abingdon_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Oxford West and Abingdon (UK Parliament constituency)">Oxford West and Abingdon</a> constituency, England.</div></div></div>
<p>Political parties are the dominant organisations in the modern UK political system.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-society_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-society-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The majority of election candidates stand on behalf of political parties of varying sizes. All parties, however large or small, must be registered with the Electoral Commission to be able to operate and stand candidates. Parties must regularly report donations, loans and spending on national elections. Larger parties must also submit audited accounts on an annual basis.
</p><p>Most parties will have an individual leader (some parties choose to nominate one or more "spokespersons" rather than having a "leader"). Leaders of the main parties will be those parties' "candidates" for the post of prime minister - though there is no formal position of "prime ministerial candidate" since the prime minister is appointed by the monarch rather than being elected directly. Where a party has members elected to a parliament, devolved assembly or local council, they will typically seek to follow a united position and maintain a disciplined group using the <a href="/wiki/Whip_(politics)" title="Whip (politics)">whip system</a>.
</p><p>Historically (until 2005, with the sole exception of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1923" title="United Kingdom general election, 1923">1923</a>), the United Kingdom has effectively had a <a href="/wiki/Two_party_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Two party system">two party system</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/First-Past-The-Post" class="mw-redirect" title="First-Past-The-Post">First-Past-The-Post</a> system used for general and local elections. <a href="/wiki/Duverger%27s_law" title="Duverger&#39;s law">Duverger's law</a> certainly seems borne out in the history of British parliamentary politics. Before World War I, the United Kingdom had a true two-party system: the main parties were the <a href="/wiki/Tory" title="Tory">Tories</a> (which became the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/British_Whig_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="British Whig Party">Whigs</a> (which became the <a href="/wiki/The_Liberal_Party_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a>), though after <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Emancipation" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Emancipation">Catholic Emancipation</a> there was also a substantial <a href="/wiki/Irish_Parliamentary_Party" title="Irish Parliamentary Party">Irish Parliamentary Party</a>. After World War II, the dominant parties have been Conservative and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>. No third party has come close to winning a parliamentary majority, although Johnston et al. wrote of the elections from 1950 to 1997, "Increasingly, a number of smaller (or third) parties has won a substantial proportion of the votes cast."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Third parties and smaller parties have always polled at least 20% of the vote between them since the 1980s, while the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> won 62 of the 646 seats in the House of Commons in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005</a>, which led some spectators to regard the Westminster Parliament as a "two and a half" party system.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>More recently, in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010</a> the share of the vote for the two largest parties fell to 65%, with seats won by several other parties, including nationalist parties. In 2015, televised <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election_debates,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election debates, 2015">election debates</a> included leaders of up to seven different parties. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">general election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (SNP) won over 90% of Scottish constituencies, to become the third party in terms of seats in the House of Commons. At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">United Kingdom Independence Party</a> won nearly 13% of the UK vote (more than double the UK-wide share obtained by the SNP) to finish third in terms of popular support, yet they won only one seat. Meanwhile, the Liberal Democrats remain the third largest political party in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, with over 100 seats.
</p><p>Smaller parties receive a higher proportion of votes, and a much higher proportion of seats, in those elections which use some form of proportional system: i.e. the regional elections for the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Assembly">Welsh Assembly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> elections. Parties, such as <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a>, the United Kingdom Independence Party and Green Parties perform better in these elections, which can therefore be considered to produce a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is relatively easy to stand for election as an independent candidate, although wins are very rare and usually involve special circumstances (for example <a href="/wiki/Martin_Bell" title="Martin Bell">Martin Bell</a>'s 1997 victory against the discredited Conservative MP <a href="/wiki/Neil_Hamilton_(politician)" title="Neil Hamilton (politician)">Neil Hamilton</a> was aided by the major parties standing aside and not contesting the election). Following the 2005 General Election there were three independent MPs, the highest number since 1945, however only one of these was returned in the 2010 election.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_candidate_selection">Parliamentary candidate selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Parliamentary candidate selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prospective_parliamentary_candidate" title="Prospective parliamentary candidate">Prospective parliamentary candidate</a></div>
<p>Almost any registered elector is entitled to stand for election to parliament, provided they are able to submit nomination forms signed by ten voters from the constituency they wish to contest, along with a £500 <a href="/wiki/Deposit_(politics)" title="Deposit (politics)">deposit</a> (which is returned to the candidate after the election if they poll more than 5% of the vote).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The selection of candidates standing for political parties is the responsibility of the party itself, and all parties follow different procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-society_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-society-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Per the <a href="/wiki/Registration_of_Political_Parties_Act_1998" title="Registration of Political Parties Act 1998">Registration of Political Parties Act 1998</a>, political party candidates must be authorised to stand for election for their party by their party's "nominating officer", or someone authorised in writing by the nominating officer.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The three largest parties, the Conservative Party, Labour Party, and Liberal Democrats, have centrally-approved lists of candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-dummies_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dummies-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>, constituency Associations select their constituency's candidates.<sup id="cite_ref-dummies_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dummies-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Central-Office-v-Burrell_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Central-Office-v-Burrell-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Some associations <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)_parliamentary_primaries" title="Conservative Party (UK) parliamentary primaries">have organised open parliamentary primaries</a>. A Constituency Association must choose a candidate using the rules approved by, and (in England, Wales and Northern Ireland) from a list established by, the Committee on Candidates of the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_the_Conservative_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Board of the Conservative Party">Board of the Conservative Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Prospective candidates apply to the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Central_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative Central Office">Conservative Central Office</a> to be included on the approved list of candidates, some candidates will be given the option of applying for any seat they choose, while others may be restricted to certain constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-personal-representation_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-personal-representation-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-costly_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costly-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> A Conservative MP can only be deselected at a special general meeting of the local Conservative association, which can only be organised if backed by a petition of more than fifty members.<sup id="cite_ref-personal-representation_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-personal-representation-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Constituency_Labour_Party" title="Constituency Labour Party">Constituency Labour Parties</a> (CLP) select the parliamentary general election candidates using procedures agreed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Executive_Committee" title="National Executive Committee">National Executive Committee</a> (NEC). The selection will always involve a "one member, one vote" ballot where all members of the CLP are entitled to select their candidate from a shortlist. The methods used to draw up the shortlist will vary according to the structure of the CLP, the time available before the election, and the number of candidates who express an interest in the selection. All selected candidates must attend and pass an interview conducted on behalf of the NEC - most candidates will do this before starting to apply for selections, though the interview can occur after a candidate is selected. Different procedures apply when a sitting Labour MP indicates they wish to stand for re-selection. On very rare occasions, the NEC may withdraw their endorsement of a candidate (including sitting MPs) after the selection process is complete. They exercised this power with regards to some of the MPs involved in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_parliamentary_expenses_scandal" title="United Kingdom parliamentary expenses scandal">expenses scandal</a> prior to the 2010 General Election.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> operate an assessment process for members wishing to join the party's list of potential candidates. Once on the list, candidates are free to apply for selection in any constituency. The candidate in each seat is selected by local party members following a hustings.<sup id="cite_ref-costly_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costly-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">United Kingdom Independence Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a> select their candidates in a similar manner to the Liberal Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-costly_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costly-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party's</a> selections are open to all members to apply. Applicants are not shortlisted, so local parties vote directly on the full list of applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-costly_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costly-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Polling_procedure">Polling procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Polling procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A person may only cast a vote if he or she is on the Electoral Register - even if he or she would otherwise qualify to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> If, because of a clerical error, someone's name has been left off the Electoral Register (even though a correctly completed application form was submitted by the deadline), the Electoral Registration Officer can amend the Register up to 9pm on polling day. Because the franchise between electors varies (for example, EU citizens who are not Commonwealth or Irish citizens cannot vote in UK Parliamentary elections) ballot papers are only issued after checking the marker in the Electoral Register before an elector's name to identify in which elections the individual is eligible to vote.
</p><p>Votes can be cast either in person at a polling station, by post or by proxy. <a href="/wiki/British_citizens" class="mw-redirect" title="British citizens">British citizens</a> residing abroad and registered as overseas electors cannot vote at British high commissions, embassies or consulates - their votes can only be cast either in person in the constituency where they are enrolled in the United Kingdom, by proxy (who must reside in and be eligible to vote in the UK) or by post (although this option is less popular as postal ballot packs are only despatched by returning officers at 4pm, 19 working days before polling day at the earliest and must be received by the returning officer by the close of poll to be counted).<sup id="cite_ref-ECabsentvotingguidance_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECabsentvotingguidance-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_person">In person</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: In person">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Polling_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Polling station">Polling stations</a> (also known as polling places) are open from 7am to 10pm on polling day.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Voters receive a poll card from the <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">returning officer</a> at their local authority with details of their allocated polling place. They are not required to show their poll card (unless they are an <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_elector#United_Kingdom" title="Anonymous elector">anonymous elector</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-representation2_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-representation2-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>) or any other form of identification at the polling place in order to vote, except in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, where one piece of photographic ID (current or expired) must be presented at the polling station - a <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Electoral_Identity_Card" title="Northern Ireland Electoral Identity Card">NI Electoral Identity Card</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Driving_licence_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Driving licence in the United Kingdom">photographic NI or GB</a> or <a href="/wiki/European_driving_licence" title="European driving licence">other EEA</a> driving licence, a <a href="/wiki/British_passport" title="British passport">British</a> or <a href="/wiki/Passports_of_the_European_Union" title="Passports of the European Union">other EU passport</a>, a Translink 60+ SmartPass, a Translink Senior SmartPass, a Translink Blind Person's SmartPass or a Translink War Disabled SmartPass.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 7am when the poll opens, the presiding officer must show the empty <a href="/wiki/Ballot_box" title="Ballot box">ballot box</a> to those who are present inside the <a href="/wiki/Polling_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Polling station">polling station</a>, before closing and sealing it.<sup id="cite_ref-PollingStationStaffHandbook_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PollingStationStaffHandbook-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having verified and marked off the voter's name and address on the list of electors, the presiding officer or poll clerk issues the <a href="/wiki/Ballot_paper" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballot paper">ballot paper</a>, calling out the voter's name, elector number and polling district reference,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> unless the voter is an <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_elector#United_Kingdom" title="Anonymous elector">anonymous elector</a>, in which case only his/her elector number is called out.<sup id="cite_ref-representation2_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-representation2-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Ballot papers cannot be issued before 7am and can only be issued after 10pm to a voter who was present in the queue at/outside the polling station at 10pm.<sup id="cite_ref-pollingstationhandbook_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingstationhandbook-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> All ballot papers contain both an official mark (e.g. a watermark or perforation) and a unique identifying number; any papers issued without both these features (even if it is the presiding officer/poll clerk's mistake) will be invalid and rejected at the count. On a separate list (called the corresponding number list) the presiding officer or poll clerk writes the voter's elector number next to the unique identifying number of the ballot paper issued. However, the <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secrecy of the vote</a> is usually maintained, as at the close of the poll this list linking voters to their ballot paper numbers is sealed inside a packet which may only be opened by the order of a court in the event that the election result is challenged. The ballot paper is folded and then handed to the voter.
</p><p>The voter marks the ballot papers in the privacy of a <a href="/wiki/Voting_booth" title="Voting booth">voting booth</a>. Polling stations must provide a writing implement for voters; usually pencils are provided (for practical reasons, as ink pens may dry out or spill), but there is no legal requirement for voters to mark their ballot papers with a pencil (they can use their own pen instead).<sup id="cite_ref-pollingstationhandbook_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingstationhandbook-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> If the ballot paper has been <a href="/wiki/Spoilt_vote" title="Spoilt vote">spoilt</a>, the presiding officer/poll clerk can issue a new one after the old ballot paper is cancelled. Before placing the ballot papers in the <a href="/wiki/Ballot_box" title="Ballot box">ballot box</a>, the voter has (in theory) to show the presiding officer or the poll clerk the official mark and the unique identifying number printed on the reverse of the ballot papers.
</p><p>If a voter requests a ballot paper but someone has already voted in their name, or they are listed as having requested a postal vote, they can only cast a <b>tendered ballot</b>. After marking the tendered ballot in private, the voter must not place it in the ballot box. Instead, it must be returned to the presiding officer who will endorse it with the voter's name, elector number and polling district reference, before placing it in a special envelope. The voter's name and elector number is then written down in the 'List of Tendered Votes'. Although tendered ballots are not included at the count, they serve as a formal record that a voter has tried, but has been unable, to cast a vote and is evidence of a voter's concern about the conduct of an election. If a voter wants to make a complaint, marking a tendered ballot is the first step in pursuing the complaints procedure.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Voters may bring their underage children with them inside the polling station, but they may only observe the voting procedure and are not permitted to participate (for example, by marking the voter's ballot paper).<sup id="cite_ref-PollingStationStaffHandbook_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PollingStationStaffHandbook-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The presiding officer and the poll clerk(s) are responsible for maintaining order in the polling station (this includes ensuring that candidates/agents/tellers in the vicinity of the polling station do not interfere with the election process and/or impede voters' access to/from the polling station, and removing any campaign literature from inside the polling station) and ensuring the secrecy and security of all ballots cast. They are under a duty to act impartially at all times.<sup id="cite_ref-pollingstationhandbook_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingstationhandbook-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Candidates may appoint <a href="/wiki/Polling_agent" title="Polling agent">polling agents</a> to observe the voting process in polling stations.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Teller_(elections)#United_Kingdom" title="Teller (elections)">Tellers</a> are often present outside the polling station and record the elector number (as it appears on the Electoral Register and poll card) of those who have voted. Tellers volunteer on behalf of political parties (identifiable by their <a href="/wiki/Rosette_(politics)" title="Rosette (politics)">rosette</a>), but have no legal or official status, and voters are not obliged to give them their elector number.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> By recording who has voted, tellers help their parties identify supporters who have not yet voted, so that they can be contacted and encouraged to vote, and offered assistance — such as transport to the polling station — if necessary.
</p><p>At the close of poll, the slot at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Ballot_box" title="Ballot box">ballot box</a> is sealed by the presiding officer or poll clerk (the election and polling agents appointed by candidates can also apply their own seals to the boxes) before being transported 'directly and without delay' by the presiding officer to the central counting location.<sup id="cite_ref-pollingstationhandbook_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingstationhandbook-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_post">By post</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: By post">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Postal_voting_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Postal voting in the United Kingdom">Postal voting in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>Voters can apply to receive a postal ballot either for specific elections or on a permanent basis until further notice without having to give a reason (except in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, where voters have to give a specific reason explaining why they cannot physically attend their allocated polling station<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>). Applications for postal ballots close at 5pm 11 working days before polling day. Postal ballots can be sent anywhere within and outside the United Kingdom, although if they are not sent to a voter's registered address, a reason must be provided to the Electoral Registration Officer as to why the postal ballot is to be sent to an alternative address.
</p><p>The returning officer must issue and send out postal ballot packs 'as soon as is practicable' (i.e. as soon as possible after the close of nominations at 4pm 19 working days before polling day).<sup id="cite_ref-ECabsentvotingguidance_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECabsentvotingguidance-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Where an elector has applied for a postal ballot to be sent to an overseas address, the returning officer should prioritise the dispatch of their postal ballot packs (over those sent to UK addresses), send them by <a href="/wiki/Air_mail" class="mw-redirect" title="Air mail">air mail</a> and ensure that the postal ballot pack includes a return envelope with sufficient postage to be sent to the UK from abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Voters return their postal ballots together with postal voting statements filled in with their date of birth and signature either by post or by hand directly to the returning officer, or by hand to the presiding officer on polling day at a polling station situated within the constituency/ward printed on the postal ballot return envelope. However, for the postal ballot to be counted, the returning officer (or the presiding officer if returned at a polling station) must receive the ballot paper by the close of poll (usually 10pm on polling day).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_proxy">By proxy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: By proxy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Any person who is <i>eligible</i> to vote<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> (he/she does not necessarily have to be on the Electoral Register already) can be appointed by another voter as his/her proxy, but for the proxy to be able to vote in an election the proxy application must be received by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> at the voter's local authority by 5pm 6 working days before polling day. The proxy can either vote in person, or can apply for a postal proxy vote (though a postal proxy vote application has an even earlier deadline - any such request must be received by the Electoral Registration Officer by 5pm 11 working days before polling day at the latest). A voter who has become ill or disabled after 5pm six working days before polling day can make an emergency application to vote by proxy as long as the application is received by the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Registration_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral Registration Officer">Electoral Registration Officer</a> by 5pm on polling day.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Unless a close relative, a person can only vote as a proxy on behalf of a maximum of 2 other voters in any single election in each constituency/ward.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> When applying to vote by proxy for more than one particular election, the application must be accompanied by a relevant attestation and must be justified based on one of the following reasons: blindness; other disability; employment; on an education course; registered as a service, overseas or anonymous elector.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> If only applying to vote by proxy for one particular election, the elector only needs to explain why he/she cannot vote in person, but does not need an attestation.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> If it is possible to get to the polling station from the registered address by only air or by sea, the elector can apply for a permanent proxy vote without an attestation.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, voters can only appoint another person to be their proxy if they can provide a specific reason explaining why they cannot physically attend their allocated polling station.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">Accessibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Accessibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All polling stations are legally required to be wheelchair-accessible<sup id="cite_ref-aboutmyvote.co.uk_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutmyvote.co.uk-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and be equipped with a <a href="/wiki/Tactile_voting_device" title="Tactile voting device">tactile voting device</a> and at least one large print display version of the ballot paper to assist visually impaired voters.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Though the large print version cannot be marked, it can be used for reference. Disabled voters can also request the Presiding Officer in the polling station or bring along a family member to mark their ballot papers for them if they wish. If a voter is unable to enter the polling station because of a disability, the Presiding Officer can take the ballot paper to him/her.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission</a> provides electoral registration forms in a number of foreign languages <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.aboutmyvote.co.uk/languages.aspx">[5]</a>, by law all voting materials (e.g. ballot papers) are only printed in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (and also in <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> in Wales).<sup id="cite_ref-aboutmyvote.co.uk_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutmyvote.co.uk-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_elections">General elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: General elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png/400px-UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png" width="400" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png/600px-UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png/800px-UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png 2x" data-file-width="1570" data-file-height="698" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_parliamentary_elections_from_1950_to_2017_graph.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UK parliamentary election results, 1950–2017</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_elections_overview" title="United Kingdom general elections overview">United Kingdom general elections overview</a></div>
<p>United Kingdom general elections are held following a <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Dissolution of the Parliament of the United Kingdom">dissolution of Parliament</a>. All the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of Parliament">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) forming the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a> are elected. Following the <a href="/wiki/Fixed-term_Parliaments_Act_2011" title="Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011">Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011</a>, parliamentary sessions last five years and the only way that an early election can be called is in a vote by a two-thirds majority of the House.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Under the Act, dissolution occurs automatically 25 working days before the election (previously, a minimum period of 17 working days applied). At this point, all parliamentary business ends and the role of MP ceases to exist until after polling day.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Candidates for each <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituency</a> are chosen by political parties or stand as independents. Almost all successful candidates are members of a political party, with only one independent elected in the 2010 election.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Each constituency elects one MP by the <a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a> system of election. At the 2005 general election, there were 646 constituencies, thus 646 MPs were elected to Parliament. At the 2010 election the number of MPs was 650.
</p><p>A party with an overall parliamentary majority (more seats than all the other parties combined) following an election forms the government. If no party has an outright majority, parties can seek to form coalitions. At the 2010 election, even though the Conservatives won the greatest number of seats, it would have been possible for the Liberal Democrats to form a coalition with Labour (and maybe also other, smaller parties) instead of with the Conservatives.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Situations such as these can give smaller parties considerable power: the eventual outcome of the 2010 election was effectively decided by the Liberal Democrats, while in 2017 the support of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a> allowed the Conservative Party to govern with a minority.
</p><p>The largest party not in government forms <a href="/wiki/Official_Opposition_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Official Opposition (United Kingdom)">Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timing">Timing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Timing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A general election must take place before each parliamentary term begins. Since the maximum term of a parliament is five years, the interval between successive general elections can exceed that period by no more than the combined length of the election campaign and the time for the new parliament to assemble (a total of typically around four weeks). The five years runs from the first meeting of Parliament following the election.
</p><p>After the 2010 general election, the <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron–Clegg coalition">coalition government</a> enacted the <a href="/wiki/Fixed-term_Parliaments_Act_2011" title="Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011">Fixed-term Parliaments Act 2011</a> which set fixed term parliaments of five years. Thus the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">next general election</a> was held on 7 May 2015, with subsequent elections scheduled to be held every five years thereafter on the first Thursday in May. However the Act also contains provisions for Parliament to be dissolved and an early election held if no government can be formed within 14 days after a <a href="/wiki/Motions_of_no_confidence_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Motions of no confidence in the United Kingdom">vote of no confidence</a> in the government. Similarly, the Act allows for an election to be triggered by a vote of two-thirds of MPs in the House of Commons calling for one.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> asks the <a href="/wiki/British_monarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarchy">Monarch</a> to dissolve Parliament by Royal Proclamation. The Proclamation also orders the issue of the formal Writs of Election which require an election to be held in each constituency. The election is held 17 working days after the date of the Proclamation, as regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1983" title="Representation of the People Act 1983">Representation of the People Act 1983</a>, s. 23 and Schedule 1 ("<i>Parliamentary election rules</i>"), rule 1 ("<i>Timetable</i>").
</p><p>Since 1935 every general election has been held on a Thursday. Of the 18 general elections between 1945 and 2010, five were held in May, four each in June and October, two in February and one each in March, April and July.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office" title="Cabinet Office">Cabinet Office</a> imposes <i><a href="/wiki/Purdah_(pre-election_period)" title="Purdah (pre-election period)">Purdah</a></i> before elections. This is a period of roughly six weeks in which Government Departments are not allowed to communicate with members of the public about any new or controversial Government initiatives (such as modernisation initiatives, and administrative and legislative changes).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-election">Post-election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Post-election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Voting ends at 10 pm (or once all voters present in a queue at/outside the polling station at 10 pm have cast their vote).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Presiding officers are responsible for sealing <a href="/wiki/Ballot_box" title="Ballot box">ballot boxes</a> in polling stations (<a href="/wiki/Election_agent" title="Election agent">election</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polling_agent" title="Polling agent">polling</a> agents appointed by candidates can also apply their own seals to the boxes) and transporting them 'directly and without delay' to the central counting location for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pollingstationhandbook_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollingstationhandbook-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">Returning officers</a> are required to 'take reasonable steps to begin counting ... as soon as practicable within the period of four hours starting with the close of the poll' (i.e. no later than 2 am).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In most constituencies, upon receipt by the <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">returning officer</a> at the central counting location, ballot boxes are unsealed and emptied, and ballot papers are verified and <a href="/wiki/Vote_counting" title="Vote counting">counted</a> immediately. Ballot papers are verified manually and counted by hand. The <a href="/wiki/Vote_counting" title="Vote counting">counting process</a> is observed by candidates and their agents.
</p><p>Results are declared in each individual <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituency</a> by the local <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">returning officer</a>. The earliest results are declared by about 11 pm, with most having been declared by 3 or 4 am; some constituencies do not declare their results until later the following day. Each individual <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament#United_Kingdom" title="Member of parliament">MP</a> assumes office immediately upon the declaration by the local <a href="/wiki/Returning_Officer#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Returning Officer">returning officer</a>.
</p><p>When all the results are known, or when one party achieves an absolute majority of the seats in the House of Commons, the first response comes from the current (and possibly outgoing) <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>. If a majority in the new Parliament has been achieved by their party, they remain in office without the need for reconfirmation or reappointment—no new "term" of office is started. If a majority has not been achieved, and another party has the numbers to form a government, the Prime Minister submits his/her resignation to the Monarch. The Monarch then commissions the leader of the new majority party to form a new government. The Prime Minister can try to remain in power even without a majority. The subsequent <a href="/wiki/State_Opening_of_Parliament" title="State Opening of Parliament">"Queen's Speech"</a> (giving an outline of the government's proposed legislative programme) offers a chance for the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> to cast a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence#United_Kingdom" title="Motion of no confidence">vote of confidence or no confidence</a> in the government by accepting or rejecting the Queen's Speech.
</p><p>By precedent, and in the absence of any formal written constitutional objection, the Monarch could in theory dismiss the incumbent Prime Minister and seek to appoint a replacement. However, this has not occurred since the dismissal of <a href="/wiki/William_Lamb,_2nd_Viscount_Melbourne" title="William Lamb, 2nd Viscount Melbourne">Lord Melbourne</a> in 1834, and would almost certainly trigger a constitutional crisis, similar to the <a href="/wiki/1975_Australian_constitutional_crisis" title="1975 Australian constitutional crisis">1975 Australian constitutional crisis</a>.
</p><p>The most recent <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of Prime Ministers of the United Kingdom">Prime Ministers</a> who, having failed to win a majority, opted not to resign immediately, were <a href="/wiki/Edward_Heath" title="Edward Heath">Edward Heath</a> in 1974, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> in 2010 and <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> in 2017. In 1974, after initial negotiations with the Liberal Party failed to provide a coalition deal, Heath resigned, allowing <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> to commission Labour leader <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> to form an administration. Until the Prime Minister reacts to the election result, either by deciding to remain on or by resigning, the Monarch has no role. Only if the Prime Minister resigns can the Monarch then commission someone else to form a government.
</p><p>The largest party not in government becomes the Official Opposition, known as <i>Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition</i>. Any smaller parties not in government are collectively known as "the opposition".
</p><p>After each election, having remained in power, a Prime Minister may engage in a major or minor <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_shuffle" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet shuffle">reshuffle</a> of ministers; such a reshuffle may occur at any time if the Prime Minister wishes it. Any vacancy arising in the House, due to death, ennoblement, or <a href="/wiki/Resignation_from_the_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="Resignation from the House of Commons">resignation</a> is filled by a <a href="/wiki/By-election" title="By-election">by-election</a>. The timing for this is not automatic and it can be months after the vacancy arose, or even abandoned if there is a general election due soon.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Previous_results">Previous results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Previous results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>See <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom general elections">United Kingdom general elections</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_by-elections" class="mw-redirect" title="List of UK by-elections">List of UK by-elections</a>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Devolved_parliament_and_assembly_elections">Devolved parliament and assembly elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Devolved parliament and assembly elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_Parliament_elections">Scottish Parliament elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Scottish Parliament elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> elections occur every four years to elect the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the Scottish Parliament">Members of the Scottish Parliament</a> (MSPs). The first election to the <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> Scottish Parliament that was created by the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>, was held in 1999. Elections to the Scottish Parliament are by the <a href="/wiki/Additional_Member_System" title="Additional Member System">Additional Member System</a>, which is a hybrid of <a href="/wiki/Single_member_plurality" class="mw-redirect" title="Single member plurality">single member plurality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Party_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Party list">party list</a>.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Election,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament Election, 1999">Scottish Parliament Election 1999</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament Election, 2003">Scottish Parliament Election 2003</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament Election, 2007">Scottish Parliament Election 2007</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament Election, 2011">Scottish Parliament Election 2011</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Parliament Election, 2016">Scottish Parliament Election 2016</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Welsh_Assembly_elections">Welsh Assembly elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elections_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Welsh Assembly elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
